S\u1ef1 tho\u00e1i lui tr\u01b0\u1edbc halving (Pre-Halving retrace)\n\nM\u1ed9t giai \u0111o\u1ea1n tho\u00e1i lui tr\u01b0\u1edbc halving th\u01b0\u1eddng di\u1ec5n ra xung quanh s\u1ef1 ki\u1ec7n halving ch\u00ednh (v\u00f2ng m\u00e0u xanh \u0111\u1eadm)\n\nN\u0103m 2016, giai \u0111o\u1ea1n n\u00e0y \u0111\u00e3 gi\u1ea3m s\u00e2u -38%\n\nN\u0103m 2020, giai \u0111o\u1ea1n n\u00e0y gi\u1ea3m s\u00e2u -20%\n\nS\u1ef1 tho\u00e1i lui tr\u01b0\u1edbc halving n\u00e0y khi\u1ebfn nh\u00e0 \u0111\u1ea7u t\u01b0 \u0111\u1eb7t c\u00e2u h\u1ecfi li\u1ec7u halving c\u00f3 th\u1ef1c s\u1ef1 l\u00e0 y\u1ebfu t\u1ed1 t\u0103ng gi\u00e1 hay kh\u00f4ng?\n\n4. Giai \u0111o\u1ea1n T\u00e1i t\u00edch lu\u1ef9 (Re-Accumulation)\n\nGiai \u0111o\u1ea1n tho\u00e1i lui tr\u01b0\u1edbc halving \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c theo sau b\u1edfi giai \u0111o\u1ea1n t\u00e1i t\u00edch lu\u1ef9 k\u00e9o d\u00e0i trong nhi\u1ec1u th\u00e1ng (m\u00e0u \u0111\u1ecf)\n\nNhi\u1ec1u nh\u00e0 \u0111\u1ea7u t\u01b0 b\u1ecb lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf trong giai \u0111o\u1ea1n n\u00e0y do s\u1ef1 bu\u1ed3n ch\u00e1n, kh\u00f4ng ki\u00ean nh\u1eabn v\u00e0 th\u1ea5t v\u1ecdng v\u00ec kh\u00f4ng \u0111\u1ea1t \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c k\u1ebft qu\u1ea3 mong mu\u1ed1n trong \u0111\u1ea7u t\u01b0 BTC c\u1ee7a h\u1ecd ngay sau halving\n\n5. Xu h\u01b0\u1edbng t\u0103ng c\u1ea5p t\u1ed1c (Parabolic Uptrend)\n\nKhi Bitcoin b\u1ee9t ph\u00e1 ra kh\u1ecfi khu v\u1ef1c t\u00e1i t\u00edch lu\u1ef9 v\u00e0 v\u00e0o xu h\u01b0\u1edbng t\u0103ng c\u1ea5p t\u1ed1c (m\u00e0u xanh)\n\nTrong giai \u0111o\u1ea1n n\u00e0y, Bitcoin tr\u1ea3i qua s\u1ef1 t\u0103ng tr\u01b0\u1edfng nhanh ch\u00f3ng tr\u00ean \u0111\u01b0\u1eddng \u0111\u1ebfn c\u00e1c m\u1ee9c gi\u00e1 k\u1ef7 l\u1ee5c m\u1edbi\n\n#Crypto  #Bitcoin", "replyCount": 24, "retweetCount": 0, "likeCount": 23, "quoteCount": 0, "conversationId": 1710540661081198662, "hashtags": ["BTC"], "cashtags": [], "mentionedUsers": [], "links": [], "viewCount": 344, "retweetedTweet": null, "quotedTweet": null, "place": null, "coordinates": null, "inReplyToTweetId": null, "inReplyToUser": null, "source": "<a href=\"http://twitter.com/download/android\" rel=\"nofollow\">Twitter for Android</a>", "sourceUrl": "http://twitter.com/download/android", "sourceLabel": "Twitter for Android", "media": {"photos": [{"url": "https://pbs.twimg.com/media/F70PqlrbMAAgx9i.jpg"}], "videos": [], "animated": []}, "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.Tweet"}

ROLLS-ROYCE\nKhi n\u00f3i \u0111\u1ebfn c\u00e1c h\u00e3ng xe \u00f4 t\u00f4 \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi, ta kh\u00f4ng th\u1ec3 kh\u00f4ng k\u1ec3 \u0111\u1ebfn Rolls-Royce. \u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng th\u01b0\u01a1ng hi\u1ec7u chuy\u00ean mang \u0111\u1ebfn cho gi\u1edbi th\u01b0\u1ee3ng l\u01b0u nh\u1eefng \u201cem\u201d si\u00eau xe \u0111\u1eaft gi\u00e1 nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi.\nRolls-Royce l\u00e0 h\u00e3ng xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t c\u00f3 xu\u1ea5t x\u1ee9 t\u1eeb V\u01b0\u01a1ng qu\u1ed1c Anh \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp t\u1eeb n\u0103m 1904 b\u1edfi Charles v\u00e0 Henry Royce. Th\u01b0\u01a1ng hi\u1ec7u xe n\u00e0y d\u00e0nh cho nh\u1eefng ng\u01b0\u1eddi thu\u1ed9c gi\u1edbi si\u00eau gi\u00e0u, th\u01b0\u1ee3ng l\u01b0u trong x\u00e3 h\u1ed9i.\nK\u1ec3 t\u1eeb khi ra m\u1eaft, h\u00e3ng xe \u00f4 t\u00f4 \u0111\u1eaft ti\u1ec1n nh\u1ea5t n\u00e0y \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u1ecb cho m\u00ecnh ph\u00e2n kh\u00fac kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng cao c\u1ea5p. Tuy nhi\u00ean, cho \u0111\u1ebfn t\u1eadn khi chi\u1ebfc Phantom V thu\u1ed9c s\u1ef1 s\u1edf h\u1eefu c\u1ee7a N\u1eef ho\u00e0ng Elizabeth II v\u00e0 John Lennon ra \u0111\u1eddi, Rolls-Royce m\u1edbi th\u1eadt s\u1ef1 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c gi\u1edbi si\u00eau gi\u00e0u s\u0103n \u0111\u00f3n.\nM\u1eabu \u00f4 t\u00f4 \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a Rolls-Royce l\u00e0 si\u00eau xe Rolls - Royce La Rose Noire Droptail, n\u00f3 c\u00f3 m\u1ee9c gi\u00e1 l\u00ean \u0111\u1ebfn 30 tri\u1ec7u \u0111\u00f4. \ud83e\udd72\ud83e\udd72\ud83e\udd72\n(\u1ea2nh minh h\u1ecda - m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng xe n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng)\n\n\ud83c\udf382. MAYBACH\nTh\u00e0nh l\u1eadp t\u1eeb n\u0103m 1909, Maybach l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t trong c\u00e1c h\u00e3ng xe \u00f4 t\u00f4 \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi c\u00f3 xu\u1ea5t x\u1ee9 t\u1ea1i \u0110\u1ee9c v\u00e0 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c c\u00e1c t\u00edn \u0111\u1ed3 m\u00ea xe c\u1ef1c k\u1ef3 y\u00eau th\u00edch. Hi\u1ec7n nay, Maybach \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c Mercedes-Benz mua l\u1ea1i v\u00e0 ch\u00e0o s\u00e2n v\u1edbi t\u01b0 c\u00e1ch l\u00e0 h\u00e3ng xe ph\u1ee5 c\u1ee7a Mercedes.\nT\u1eeb khi ra m\u1eaft cho \u0111\u1ebfn nay, Maybach lu\u00f4n \u0111em \u0111\u1ebfn nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng s\u1ea3n ph\u1ea9m ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng th\u01b0\u1ee3ng l\u01b0u, c\u00f3 nhi\u1ec1u ti\u1ec1n c\u1ee7a trong x\u00e3 h\u1ed9i. V\u00ec l\u1ebd \u0111\u00f3, t\u1eebng chi\u1ebfc si\u00eau xe c\u1ee7a Maybach mang \u0111\u1ebfn tay kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ec1u ph\u1ea3i tr\u1ea3i qua nh\u1eefng kh\u00e2u ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t nghi\u00eam ng\u1eb7t nh\u1ea5t.\n\u0110\u1eb7c tr\u01b0ng \u1ea5n t\u01b0\u1ee3ng c\u1ee7a Maybach thu h\u00fat c\u00e1c t\u00edn \u0111\u1ed3 m\u00ea xe b\u1edfi n\u00f3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c ho\u00e0n thi\u1ec7n ch\u1ec9n chu t\u1eeb t\u1eeb nh\u1eefng th\u1ee9 nh\u1ecf nh\u01b0 n\u01b0\u1edbc s\u01a1n cho \u0111\u1ebfn c\u00e1c \u0111i\u1ec3m quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u01b0 n\u1ed9i th\u1ea5t, \u0111\u1ed9ng c\u01a1\u2026 \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y khi\u1ebfn kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng h\u00e0i l\u00f2ng tuy\u1ec7t \u0111\u1ed1i b\u1edfi gi\u00e1 tr\u1ecb m\u00e0 si\u00eau xe Maybach mang l\u1ea1i.\nM\u1eabu xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a Maybach l\u00e0 si\u00eau xe Mercedes-Maybach Exelero v\u1edbi m\u1ee9c gi\u00e1 g\u1ea7n 10 tri\u1ec7u \u0111\u00f4.\n(\u1ea2nh minh h\u1ecda - m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng xe n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng)\n\n\ud83c\udf383. LAMBORGHINI\nN\u1ebfu l\u00e0 t\u00edn \u0111\u1ed3 c\u1ee7a phim Hollywood ho\u1eb7c nh\u1ea1c \u00c2u M\u1ef9, ch\u1eafc ch\u1eafn b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd th\u01b0\u1eddng xuy\u00ean th\u1ea5y nh\u1eefng \u201cem\u201d Lamborghini xu\u1ea5t hi\u1ec7n v\u1edbi t\u01b0 c\u00e1ch l\u00e0 ph\u01b0\u01a1ng ti\u1ec7n c\u1ee7a nh\u1eefng nh\u00e2n v\u1eadt gi\u00e0u c\u00f3, \u0111\u1eb3ng c\u1ea5p.\nTh\u00e0nh l\u1eadp v\u00e0o n\u0103m 1963 t\u1ea1i \u00dd, Lamborghini \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c bi\u1ebft \u0111\u1ebfn l\u00e0 c\u00e1c h\u00e3ng \u00f4 t\u00f4 \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi chuy\u00ean mang \u0111\u1ebfn cho kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng si\u00eau xe th\u1ec3 hi\u1ec7n \u0111\u1eb3ng c\u1ea5p v\u00e0 gi\u00e1 tr\u1ecb c\u1ee7a b\u1ea3n th\u00e2n.\nM\u1eabu xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng l\u00e0 Lamborghini Veneno. \u0110\u1ecbnh gi\u00e1 ban \u0111\u1ea7u 4,5 tri\u1ec7u \u0111\u00f4 v\u00e0 sau \u0111\u00f3 \u0111\u00e3 b\u00e1n \u0111\u1ea5u gi\u00e1 th\u00e0nh c\u00f4ng v\u1edbi m\u1ee9c gi\u00e1 8,3 tri\u1ec7u \u0111\u00f4 v\u00e0o n\u0103m 2019.\n(\u1ea2nh minh h\u1ecda - m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng xe n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng)\n\n\ud83c\udf384. FERRARI\nL\u00e0 th\u01b0\u01a1ng hi\u1ec7u s\u1ea3n xu\u1ea5t xe \u00f4 t\u00f4 h\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ea7u c\u1ee7a \u00dd, Ferrari lu\u00f4n mang \u0111\u1ebfn cho kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng nh\u1eefng chi\u1ebfc xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi, \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c c\u00e1c t\u00edn \u0111\u1ed3 m\u00ea xe \u01b0a chu\u1ed9ng v\u00e0 khao kh\u00e1t s\u1edf h\u1eefu. Th\u01b0\u01a1ng hi\u1ec7u xe \u00f4 t\u00f4 n\u00e0y th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp v\u00e0o n\u0103m 1939 b\u1edfi doanh nh\u00e2n Enzo Ferrari.\nFerrari lu\u00f4n \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111\u00e1nh gi\u00e1 cao b\u1edfi nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng xe m\u00e0 th\u01b0\u01a1ng hi\u1ec7u n\u00e0y mang \u0111\u1ebfn cho kh\u00e1ch h\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ec1u c\u00f3 thi\u1ebft k\u1ebf n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt v\u1edbi tone m\u00e0u Rosso Corsa ch\u1ee7 \u0111\u1ea1o. H\u01a1n th\u1ebf, kh\u1ea3 n\u0103ng v\u1eadn h\u00e0nh cao c\u1ea5p v\u00e0 \u1ea5n t\u01b0\u1ee3ng c\u1ee7a Ferrari c\u0169ng l\u00e0 \u0111i\u1ec3m \u0111\u1eb3ng c\u1ea5p, \u0103n ti\u1ec1n c\u1ee7a Ferrari.\nM\u1eabu xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng l\u00e0 Ferrari 250 GT0 1963. Chi\u1ebfc si\u00eau xe h\u1ec7 c\u1ed5 \u0111i\u1ec3n n\u00e0y \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c b\u00e1n v\u1edbi m\u1ee9c gi\u00e1 l\u00ean \u0111\u1ebfn 70 tri\u1ec7u \u0111\u00f4.\ud83d\ude4c\ud83d\ude4c\ud83d\ude4c\n(\u1ea2nh minh h\u1ecda - m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng d\u00f2ng xe n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt c\u1ee7a h\u00e3ng)\n\n\ud83c\udf385. BENTLEY\nBentley c\u0169ng \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c bi\u1ebft \u0111\u1ebfn l\u00e0 c\u00e1c h\u00e3ng xe h\u01a1i \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi, c\u00f3 xu\u1ea5t x\u1ee9 t\u1ea1i V\u01b0\u01a1ng qu\u1ed1c Anh v\u00e0 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp v\u00e0o n\u0103m 1919. Hi\u1ec7n nay, h\u00e3ng xe \u0111\u1eaft nh\u1ea5t th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi n\u00e0y thu\u1ed9c quy\u1ec1n s\u1edf h\u1eefu c\u1ee7a t\u1eadp \u0111o\u00e0n Volkswagen \u2013 \u0110\u1ee9c.\n\u0110i\u1ec3m \u0111\u1eb7c tr\u01b0ng khi\u1ebfn ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng d\u1ec5 d\u00e0ng nh\u1eadn di\u1ec7n ra d\u00f2ng xe cao c\u1ea5p n\u00e0y ch\u00ednh l\u00e0 logo c\u00f3 bi\u1ec3u t\u01b0\u1ee3ng ch\u1eef B tr\u00f2n g\u1ea7n gi\u1ed1ng v\u1edbi s\u1ed1 8, r\u1ea5t d\u1ec5 d\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ec3 nh\u1eadn di\u1ec7n. Th\u1ea5y m\u1ec7t, Th\u01b0 b\u00e8n th\u1ea3 Ki\u1ec1u, kh\u00f4ng ch\u00ednh th\u1ee9c th\u1ea3 m\u00e0 cho \u0111i tr\u1ed1n kh\u00f4ng b\u1eaft l\u1ea1i, ch\u1eeba \u0111\u01b0\u1eddng sau n\u00e0y, n\u1ebfu c\u00f3 g\u1eb7p l\u1ea1i nhau th\u00ec Ki\u1ec1u c\u0169ng m\u1ed9t ch\u00fat m\u1eafc c\u1ee1. Quy\u1ec1n b\u00ednh trong tay, Ki\u1ec1u b\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u b\u00e1o \u01a1n b\u00e1o o\u00e1n, sai ng\u01b0\u1eddi \u0111i b\u1eaft h\u1ebft nh\u1eefng ng\u01b0\u1eddi t\u1eebng h\u1ea1i n\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ec3 x\u1eed t\u1ed9i, m\u1eddi h\u1ebft nh\u1eefng ng\u01b0\u1eddi t\u1eebng c\u1ee9u n\u00e0ng t\u1edbi \u0111\u1ec3 b\u00e1o \u0111\u00e1p. Ki\u1ec1u t\u1ef1 m\u00ecnh th\u1ef1c hi\u1ec7n lu\u1eadt nh\u00e2n-qu\u1ea3, karma cho nhanh ch\u1ee9 kh\u00f4ng \u0111\u1ee3i tr\u1eddi xanh. V\u1edbi nh\u1eefng ng\u01b0\u1eddi kh\u00e1c th\u00ec n\u00e0ng tr\u1ecb t\u1ed9i h\u00ecnh, nh\u01b0ng t\u1edbi Th\u01b0 th\u00ec Ki\u1ec1u b\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u l\u1ea5y t\u00e0i tr\u00ed c\u1ee7a m\u00ecnh ra, \u0111\u1ed1i x\u1eed y h\u1ec7t nh\u01b0 x\u01b0a, ch\u1ec9 kh\u00e1c l\u00e0 \u0111\u1ed5i vai. Ki\u1ec1u \u0111on \u0111\u1ea3 xin ch\u00e0o ti\u1ec3u th\u01b0, kh\u00f4ng ng\u1edd c\u0169ng c\u00f3 ng\u00e0y g\u1eb7p l\u1ea1i nhau, \u1edf v\u1ecb tr\u00ed n\u00e0y c\u0169ng th\u1eadt l\u00e0 oan tr\u00e1i. Ki\u1ec1u khen Th\u01b0 l\u00e0:\n\n\"\u0110\u00e0n b\u00e0 d\u1ec5 c\u00f3 m\u1ea5y tay\n\u0110\u1eddi x\u01b0a m\u1ea5y m\u1eb7t \u0111\u1eddi n\u00e0y m\u1ea5y gan!\nD\u1ec5 d\u00e0ng l\u00e0 th\u00f3i h\u1ed3ng nhan\nC\u00e0ng cay nghi\u1ec7t l\u1eafm c\u00e0ng oan tr\u00e1i nhi\u1ec1u\u201d. \n\n\u0110\u00e1p l\u1ea1i, Th\u01b0 nh\u1ecf nh\u1eb9 nh\u1eafc kh\u00e9o Ki\u1ec1u v\u1ec1 vi\u1ec7c cho n\u00e0ng \u0111i ra C\u00e1c \u0111\u1ec3 vi\u1ebft kinh, r\u1ed3i \u0111o\u1ea1n \u0111i tr\u1ed1n m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng \u0111u\u1ed5i b\u1eaft l\u1ea1i \"Ngh\u0129 cho khi c\u00e1c vi\u1ebft kinh. V\u1edbi khi kh\u1ecfi c\u1eeda - d\u1ee9t t\u00ecnh ch\u1eb3ng theo\". Ki\u1ec1u ch\u1ee3t nh\u1edb v\u1ee5 m\u00ecnh c\u00f3 \u0103n c\u1eafp m\u1ed9t \u00edt ti\u1ec1n b\u1ea1c nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0 khi ch\u1ea1y tr\u1ed1n, n\u00ean th\u1ea5y ng\u01b0\u1ee3ng. Th\u01b0 kh\u00f4ng n\u00f3i v\u1ee5 \u0103n c\u1eafp, v\u00ec s\u1ee3 Ki\u1ec1u b\u1ebd m\u1eb7t, ch\u1ec9 nh\u1eafc s\u01a1 v\u1eady th\u00f4i. Th\u01b0 ch\u1ec9 n\u00f3i v\u1ec1 b\u1ea3n th\u00e2n m\u00ecnh, \"r\u1eb1ng t\u00f4i CH\u00daT PH\u1eacN \u0110\u00c0N B\u00c0, ghen tu\u00f4ng th\u00ec c\u0169ng ng\u01b0\u1eddi ta th\u01b0\u1eddng t\u00ecnh, ch\u1ed3ng chung ch\u01b0a d\u1ec5 ai chi\u1ec1u cho ai\". Sau m\u00e0n b\u00e0o ch\u1eefa tuy\u1ec7t v\u1eddi \u0111\u00f3, Ho\u1ea1n Th\u1ef1 kh\u1ea5u \u0111\u1ea7u xin l\u01b0\u1ee3ng th\u1ee9, b\u1ea3o gi\u1edd m\u00ecnh l\u00e0 c\u00e1 n\u1eb1m tr\u00ean th\u1edbt, n\u00e0ng \u0111\u00e3 l\u00e0 phu nh\u00e2n cao qu\u00fd, quy\u1ebft sao c\u0169ng \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c. Ki\u1ec1u nghe v\u1eady n\u00ean tha b\u1ed5ng, m\u00ecnh c\u0169ng l\u00e0 ng\u01b0\u1eddi \u0111\u1eb3ng c\u1ea5p, n\u1ebfu l\u00e0m qu\u00e1 th\u00ec s\u1ebd \"th\u00e0nh ng\u01b0\u1eddi nh\u1ecf nhen\". \n\nTh\u01b0 l\u00e0 ng\u01b0\u1eddi duy nh\u1ea5t \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c Ki\u1ec1u tha v\u00ec m\u00e0n t\u1ef1 b\u00e0o ch\u1eefa xu\u1ea5t s\u1eafc, Ki\u1ec1u v\u1eabn cho r\u1eb1ng Th\u01b0 l\u00e0 ng\u01b0\u1eddi ph\u1ee5 n\u1eef t\u00e0i n\u0103ng v\u00e0 r\u1ea5t \u0111\u1eddi. Ng\u01b0\u1eddi x\u01b0a, khi n\u00f3i v\u1ec1 c\u00e1i ghen c\u1ee7a ph\u1ee5 n\u1eef, c\u00f3 c\u00e2u \"\u1edbt n\u00e0o m\u00e0 \u1edbt ch\u1eb3ng cay, g\u00e1i n\u00e0o m\u00e0 g\u00e1i ch\u1eb3ng hay ghen ch\u1ed3ng\". Nh\u01b0ng \u0111\u00f3 l\u00e0 ng\u00e0y x\u01b0a, b\u00e2y gi\u1edd nhi\u1ec1u \u1edbt \u0111\u00e2u c\u00f3 cay (\u1edbt chu\u00f4ng \u0110\u00e0 L\u1ea1t ch\u1eb3ng h\u1ea1n), n\u00ean b\u00e2y gi\u1edd g\u00e1i sang ch\u1eb3ng th\u00e8m ghen n\u1eefa. G\u1eb7p m\u1ea5y th\u1eb1ng t\u00e0o lao, h\u00e8n h\u00e8n nh\u01b0 Th\u00fac Sinh l\u00e0 Next, please! (m\u1eddi \u0111i, m\u1eddi ng\u01b0\u1eddi kh\u00e1c \u0111\u1ebfn). Ch\u1ec9 c\u00f2n g\u00e1i k\u00e9m t\u1ef1 tin, ph\u1ee5 thu\u1ed9c ti\u1ec1n b\u1ea1c th\u00ec m\u1edbi s\u1ee3 m\u1ea5t, m\u1edbi tranh gi\u00e0nh, m\u1edbi ghen. V\u1edb v\u1ea9n l\u00e0 cho l\u00ean \u0111\u01b0\u1eddng ngay, kh\u00f4ng t\u1ed1n n\u01b0\u1edbc m\u1eaft kh\u00f3c l\u00f3c van xin t\u00ecnh c\u1ea3m. B\u1ecf xong th\u00ec \u0111i spa l\u00e0m \u0111\u1eb9p, \u0111i du l\u1ecbch vui ch\u01a1i. Gi\u1ecfi n\u1eefa th\u00ec v\u1ec1 qu\u00ea m\u1edf nh\u00e0 m\u00e1y x\u00ed nghi\u1ec7p xu\u1ea5t kh\u1ea9u l\u1ea5y \u0111\u00f4 la, T\u00e2y T\u00e0u n\u00f3 bu theo, tha h\u1ed3 ch\u1ecdn, to\u00e0n doanh nh\u00e2n qu\u1ed1c t\u1ebf x\u1ecbn.\n\nTr\u00ed tu\u1ec7 d\u00f9ng \u0111\u1ec3 ki\u1ebfm ti\u1ec1n, \u0111\u1ea5u tr\u00ed gi\u00e0nh ch\u1ed3ng nh\u01b0 c\u00e1i Th\u01b0 trong \u0111o\u1ea1n v\u0103n tr\u00ean th\u00ec h\u01a1i u\u1ed5ng. {"id": 1710128354895286781, "id_str": "1710128354895286781", "url": "https://twitter.com/Blogtravelasia/status/1710128354895286781", "date": "2023-10-06 03:02:27+00:00", "user": {"id": 1692126822195171328, "id_str": "1692126822195171328", "url": "https://twitter.com/Blogtravelasia", "username": "Blogtravelasia", "displayname": "WanderlustJourney", "rawDescription": "It's a passionate traveler \ud83c\udf0d\u2708\ufe0f | Love to exploring the beauty of Vietnam & Asia. Join me as I uncover hidden treasures, share travel tips, and embrace diverse", "created": "2023-08-17 10:51:25+00:00", "followersCount": 1032, "friendsCount": 837, "statusesCount": 3324, "favouritesCount": 4128, "listedCount": 0, "mediaCount": 203, "location": "", "profileImageUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_images/1692127431195611136/_shmj8fw_normal.jpg", "profileBannerUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_banners/1692126822195171328/1692276362", "protected": null, "verified": false, "blue": true, "blueType": null, "descriptionLinks": [], "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.User"}, "lang": "en", "rawContent": "Ha Nam, a serene region located to the south of the capital city, boasts pleasant weather and is blessed with numerous natural attractions. It is not only renowned for its long-standing cultural heritage but is also gaining recognition for its spiritual sites, particularly four famous temples: Tam Chuc, Ba Danh, Phat Quang, and Dia Tang Phi Lai. Though it seemed to have been forgotten by time, the temple named Dia Tang has recently undergone a transformation, attracting numerous travelers from afar to pay their respects and enjoy its scenic beauty. The sense of tranquility at the temple gate, the peaceful beauty, and the simplicity of the surroundings make one feel at ease, as if they are free from worldly troubles.\n\nChua Dia Tang Phi Lai, also known as Chua Dung in local folklore, originated from the ancient name \"Dung\" of Ninh Trung village in Thanh Liem district, Ha Nam province. Local residents pass down the story that the temple was built in the 11th century and consists of over 100 chambers. In the past, King Tran Nghe Tong chose the temple as his place of retreat, and King Tu Duc also visited the temple to seek solace.\n\nAs of now, the temple is nearly a thousand years old and has gradually deteriorated over time. It wasn't until the end of 2015 that Venerable Thich Minh Quang began to undertake restoration efforts and gave it a new name, Dia Tang Phi Lai Tu, signifying that Bodhisattva Dia Tang V\u01b0\u01a1ng had come to this place, attained Buddhahood, and did not return. The ancient temple is situated on a hill overlooking vast rice fields, nestled against a pine-covered hill, surrounded by nature in all four directions. Perhaps this is one of the reasons why the temple was abandoned for a long time, as its remote and lush surroundings made it difficult to access before its renovation and subsequent recognition by tourists today.\n\nHow much does it cost to enter Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nCurrently, Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple does not charge an entrance fee. You can enter the temple grounds freely. Despite recent renovations and improvements, the temple does not charge any fees to Buddhist followers or visitors who come for sightseeing. On hot days, the monks at the temple even lend visitors traditional palm-leaf hats to shield them from the sun and offer them the opportunity to take photographs. If you happen to forget to wear appropriate attire, you can also ask for robes available at the temple.\n\nWhen is the best time to visit Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nThe temple is particularly beautiful during the Lunar New Year, with vibrant flowers adorning its premises. Around the 9th to 10th day of the Lunar New Year, the temple recreates the atmosphere of a traditional Northern Delta countryside market with various distinctive stalls. On important occasions, the temple also organizes many activities, providing an opportunity for both Buddhist devotees and pilgrims to visit. The Vu Lan Festival is celebrated on the 30th of the seventh lunar month, the Mid-Autumn Festival on the 15th of the eighth lunar month, and a special summer retreat program takes place from June to July, allowing those interested in temporarily leaving their daily lives behind to live and engage in spiritual activities alongside the monks, performing good deeds and listening to sermons.\n\nDirections and How to Reach Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple\n is located about 70 kilometers south of Hanoi, and there are two convenient routes for both cars and motorcycles:\n\nBy car: Depart from Hanoi and head towards the Cau Gie - Ninh Binh expressway, leading to Phu Ly, Ha Nam, via National Highway 1A. From there, continue straight for about 12 kilometers, and you'll arrive at the temple. The journey by car takes approximately 1.5 hours.\n\nBy motorcycle: From Hanoi, head to Nuoc Ngam Bus Station, then follow National Highway 1A (the old route) to Van Dien, Thuong Tin, Van Dien Train Station, Phu Xuyen, Cau Gie, and Phu Ly City. Follow Provincial Road 495 to reach the temple. This motorcycle route allows you to experience the scenic countryside and may take around 2 to 2.5 hours, depending on your starting point in Hanoi.\n\nWhat to See and Do at Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nDia Tang Phi Lai Temple offers a serene and tranquil environment for visitors. The temple's perfect blend of architecture and nature creates a unique atmosphere. Behind it lies a lush forest, while nearby, there is a small peaceful pond. Inside the temple grounds, you'll find various types of flowers and plants commonly associated with Buddhist settings. Instead of the moss-covered ancient look, the temple features a calm, subdued brown color, evoking a sense of serenity and detachment from worldly affairs. There's no hustle and bustle, no dust, and it's far removed from the chaos of urban life. Pilgrims and travelers alike come here to find a place of tranquility where they can connect with nature, surrounded by Buddhist devotees and the temple's peaceful ambiance.\n\nKh\u1ed5 H\u1ea3i and the 12 Circles: Passing through the temple gate and entering the courtyard, you'll be pleasantly surprised by the extensive white stone pavement. Instead of the typical red brick flooring found in most temples, Dia Tang is paved with white stones. Adjacent to the courtyard is a sign that reads \"Kh\u1ed5 h\u1ea3i,\" which means \"sea of suffering.\" The 12 circles drawn on the white stones in front of the main hall represent the 12 links of dependent origination, symbolizing meditation practice. All of these elements are clear and deeply connected to the teachings of Buddhism.\n\nDifferent Areas within the Temple: Like many traditional temples in the Red River Delta, Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple features traditional architectural elements such as wooden columns and curved roofs with intricate carvings. The most prominent structure within the temple complex is Tam Bao, which is the largest hall dedicated to Bodhisattva Dia Tang. To the right of this hall is the Ancestors' Hall, where 42 founding monks of the temple are venerated. Additionally, there is a small temple dedicated to Bodhisattva Quan The Am, Lord, and Saint Hien. The temple also provides accommodation for monks, Buddhist followers staying at the temple, a lecture hall for daily teachings by the resident monk, and a guesthouse for travelers and participants in temple activities.\n\nView Ancient L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n Dynasty Artifacts: The temple houses nearly 100 ceramic, porcelain, and earthenware artifacts with diverse colors, patterns, and motifs, which are identified as relics from the Tran era, with a few rare pieces from the L\u00fd and L\u00ea dynasties. Among them, many roof tiles are engraved with intricate lotus patterns, dragon motifs, and phoenix designs, along with the two parts of a mythical creature that symbolizes historical continuity from the L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n era.\n\nThe Path to the Mountain Peak: Conquering the temple's mountain peaks through the steep and challenging path along a stream requires determination. It includes rope-assisted climbs and passages through caves. Along the way, there are nearly 20 resting points for travelers. Meditation gardens are adorned with white stones or lush green grass, providing a space for tea enjoyment, relaxation, and panoramic views of the temple from above. At the Phi Lai peak, you will also find the Pho Dong Tower, built during the L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n era, which serves as a resting place for 40 generations of Zen masters.\n\nTips and Etiquette for Visiting Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple:\n\nDress appropriately: Before visiting the temple, ensure you are dressed modestly and avoid revealing attire, as it shows respect for the sacredness of the place. If you forget to wear suitable clothing, you can borrow robes provided by the temple.\n\nRespect temple property: All items and areas within the temple grounds are considered sacred. Do not touch or take any items without the permission of the temple authorities.\n\nOffering donations: Instead of offering money directly to the Buddha statues or altars, it is recommended to place your donation in the designated donation box for accumulating merit.\n\nGreetings: Show respect to the monks and nuns by greeting them with a polite gesture of placing your palms together and bowing.\n\nPhotography: You are generally allowed to take photographs within the temple grounds, but if you plan to use specialized equipment or fly drones for aerial shots, it's advisable to seek permission from the temple management.\n\nChua Dia Tang Phi Lai T\u1ef1 is a spiritual haven that has become an integral part of the lives of the people of Ninh Trung and Liem Son, as well as a spiritual pilgrimage site for visitors from afar. On the first day of each month, on full moon days, or during Buddhist holidays, people from all walks of life visit the temple to offer incense and seek peace and good health, a tradition that has persisted for many years.\n\nDia Tang Phi Lai Temple also plays a significant role in hosting weddings. Couples who choose to marry at the temple are embracing deep spiritual meaning. It's a practice that signifies respect for Buddhist traditions and emphasizes harmony, compassion, and love\u2014an ethos that Buddhism encourages.\n\nThe H\u1eb1ng Thu\u1eadn Festival, celebrated at Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple, is an important occasion for the Buddhist community to gather and engage in spiritual practice. This festival typically takes place on the 1st day of the 1st lunar month each year, coinciding with an anniversary in the life of the Buddha.
